# RPCE Practice Questions (generated, RONR 12th-ed.-grounded)

1000 questions across 638 concepts. Types are varied so the same fact resurfaces in different shapes (cloze with hints, applied multiple choice, order-of-precedence ranking and ordering, and motion-characteristic questions). Every question is answerable from what it shows; the RONR (12th ed.) section is cited only in the answer.

Counts by type: Amendability (18), Applied multiple-choice (365), Cloze recall (365), Debatability (18), Order of precedence (ordering) (99), Order of precedence (ranking) (99), Second required (18), Vote required (18)

> Reproduce with `python pylib/tools/rpce_generate_questions.py`.

## Domain 1: Motions in General and Main Motions

**1.** `[K0051 · Second required]` Does the motion to Main Motion require a second?
   A. Requires a second
   B. No second required

   *Answer:* Requires a second. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:1 — “As explained in 3–6, a main motion is a motion whose introduction brings business before the assembly; such a motion can be made only while no other motion is pending.”

**2.** `[K0049 · Vote required]` What vote does the motion to Main Motion require to be adopted?
   A. Majority vote
   B. Two-thirds vote
   C. No vote (chair rules / demand)
   D. Unanimous consent

   *Answer:* Majority vote. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:1 — “As explained in 3–6, a main motion is a motion whose introduction brings business before the assembly; such a motion can be made only while no other motion is pending.”

**3.** `[K0052 · Amendability]` Can the motion to Main Motion be amended?
   A. Amendable
   B. Not amendable

   *Answer:* Amendable. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:1 — “As explained in 3–6, a main motion is a motion whose introduction brings business before the assembly; such a motion can be made only while no other motion is pending.”

**4.** `[K0050 · Debatability]` Is the motion to Main Motion debatable?
   A. Debatable
   B. Not debatable

   *Answer:* Debatable. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:1 — “As explained in 3–6, a main motion is a motion whose introduction brings business before the assembly; such a motion can be made only while no other motion is pending.”

**5.** `[C0026 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The division of main motions into _____ and _____ main motions was mentioned in 6 and is discussed below.

   *Answer:* original, incidental — “The division of main motions into original and incidental main motions was mentioned in 6 and is discussed below.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:2 — “The division of main motions into original and incidental main motions was mentioned in 6 and is discussed below.”

**6.** `[C0026 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: The division of main motions into _____ and incidental main motions was mentioned in 6 and is discussed below.
   A. Withdraw or Modify a Motion
   B. Regular
   C. interrupted
   D. original

   *Answer:* D) original. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:2 — “The division of main motions into original and incidental main motions was mentioned in 6 and is discussed below.”

**7.** `[C0042 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The word “_____” is underlined or printed in italics, and is followed by a comma and the word “That”—which begins with a capital “T.” If there is more than one resolving clause, each of them should be a separate paragraph.

   *Answer:* Resolved, Resolved — “The word “Resolved” is underlined or printed in italics, and is followed by a comma and the word “That”—which begins with a capital “T.” If there is more than one resolving clause, each of them should be a separate paragraph.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:22 — “The word “Resolved” is underlined or printed in italics, and is followed by a comma and the word “That”—which begins with a capital “T.” If there is more than one resolving clause, each of them should be a separate paragraph.”

**8.** `[C0042 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: The word “_____” is underlined or printed in italics, and is followed by a comma and the word “That”—which begins with a capital “T.” If there is more than one resolving clause, each of them should be a separate paragraph.
   A. main
   B. Resolved
   C. Consideration by Paragraph or Seriatim
   D. Standing

   *Answer:* B) Resolved. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:22 — “The word “Resolved” is underlined or printed in italics, and is followed by a comma and the word “That”—which begins with a capital “T.” If there is more than one resolving clause, each of them should be a separate paragraph.”

**9.** `[C0043 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): For example, “A Point of Order yields to the motion to _____, and to all privileged motions.” This statement is true without qualification if the point of order is in connection with a motion ranking lower than _____ (that is, a main motion or any other subsidiary motion);

   *Answer:* Lay on the Table, Lay on the Table — “For example, “A Point of Order yields to the motion to Lay on the Table, and to all privileged motions.” This statement is true without qualification if the point of order is in connection with a motion ranking lower than Lay on the Table (that is, a main motion or any other subsidiary motion);”. See RONR (12th ed.) 6:21 — “For example, “A Point of Order yields to the motion to Lay on the Table, and to all privileged motions.” This statement is true without qualification if the point of order is in connection with a motion ranking lower than Lay on the Table (that is, a main motion or any other subsidiary motion);”

**10.** `[C0043 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: but a point of order arising from a motion to Recess would yield only to the two higher-ranking privileged motions—to Adjourn and to _____ Adjourn.
   A. Form and
   B. Fix the Time to Which to
   C. Suspend the Rules
   D. in the brief interval

   *Answer:* B) Fix the Time to Which to. See RONR (12th ed.) 6:21 — “but a point of order arising from a motion to Recess would yield only to the two higher-ranking privileged motions—to Adjourn and to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn.”

**11.** `[C0047 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): A subsidiary or incidental motion _____ to a main question if it is related to the main question in such a way that—once introduced—it must be decided before the main question can be decided.

   *Answer:* adhere — “A subsidiary or incidental motion adhere to a main question if it is related to the main question in such a way that—once introduced—it must be decided before the main question can be decided.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:35 — “A subsidiary or incidental motion adhere to a main question if it is related to the main question in such a way that—once introduced—it must be decided before the main question can be decided.”

**12.** `[C0059 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): To Call for the Orders of the Day (18) and to _____ of Privilege (19) each have privileged rank and can therefore interrupt pending business.

   *Answer:* Raise a Question — “To Call for the Orders of the Day (18) and to Raise a Question of Privilege (19) each have privileged rank and can therefore interrupt pending business.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:36 — “To Call for the Orders of the Day (18) and to Raise a Question of Privilege (19) each have privileged rank and can therefore interrupt pending business.”

**13.** `[C0059 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: Certain questions may come before the assembly with the status of main motions after having interrupted other business, however, if they are brought up by means of either of the two lowest-ranking _____ motions.
   A. even if it is
   B. prevent consideration
   C. privileged
   D. executive session

   *Answer:* C) privileged. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:36 — “Certain questions may come before the assembly with the status of main motions after having interrupted other business, however, if they are brought up by means of either of the two lowest-ranking privileged motions.”

**14.** `[C0074 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): All of them take precedence over motions of any other class (except in certain instances where the immediately pending question may be a motion to _____, a motion for the _____, or an incidental motion that was moved while a still higher-ranking privileged motion was immediately pending).

   *Answer:* Amend, Previous Question — “All of them take precedence over motions of any other class (except in certain instances where the immediately pending question may be a motion to Amend, a motion for the Previous Question, or an incidental motion that was moved while a still higher-ranking privileged motion was immediately pending).”. See RONR (12th ed.) 6:11 — “All of them take precedence over motions of any other class (except in certain instances where the immediately pending question may be a motion to Amend, a motion for the Previous Question, or an incidental motion that was moved while a still higher-ranking privileged motion was immediately pending).”

**15.** `[C0074 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: All of them take precedence over motions of any other class (except in certain instances where the immediately pending question may be a motion to Amend, a motion for the _____, or an incidental motion that was moved while a still higher-ranking privileged motion was immediately pending).

   B. Previous Question
   C. demand
   D. Unfinished

   *Answer:* B) Previous Question. **16.** `[C0148 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): A preamble consists of one or more clauses beginning “Whereas,.…” _____ rule nor custom requires a resolution to have a preamble, and one should not be used merely for the sake of form.

   *Answer:* It should be emphasized that neither — “A preamble consists of one or more clauses beginning “Whereas,.…” It should be emphasized that neither rule nor custom requires a resolution to have a preamble, and one should not be used merely for the sake of form.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:16 — “A preamble consists of one or more clauses beginning “Whereas,.…” It should be emphasized that neither rule nor custom requires a resolution to have a preamble, and one should not be used merely for the sake of form.”

**17.** `[C0148 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: When special circumstances make it desirable to include a brief statement of background, the motion should be cast in the form of a resolution, with the background or reasons incorporated in a _____ that is placed before the resolving clauses.
   A. brought before the assembly
   B. dilatory
   C. ruling
   D. preamble

   *Answer:* D) preamble. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:16 — “When special circumstances make it desirable to include a brief statement of background, the motion should be cast in the form of a resolution, with the background or reasons incorporated in a preamble that is placed before the resolving clauses.”

   *Answer:* Amend Something Previously Adopted, Discharge a Committee — “Motions that have the effect of changing or nullifying previous action of the assembly—such as the motion to Rescind or to Amend Something Previously Adopted (35), the motion to Discharge a Committee (36), or a motion to postpone an event already scheduled—require previous notice if they are to be adopted by only a majority vote.”. **44.** `[C0678 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): In organizations with employees, the assembly or the board can give instructions to an employee in the form of an _____, which is written just as a resolution except that the word “_____” is used in place of the word “Resolved.” An example would be: “Ordered, That the steward obtain impoundment of all unauthorized vehicles found parked on the club premises.”

   *Answer:* order, Ordered — “In organizations with employees, the assembly or the board can give instructions to an employee in the form of an order, which is written just as a resolution except that the word “Ordered” is used in place of the word “Resolved.” An example would be: “Ordered, That the steward obtain impoundment of all unauthorized vehicles found parked on the club premises.””. **46.** `[C0699 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): Subsidiary motions as a class are distinguished by having all _____ of the following characteristics: (1) They are always _____ to another motion while it is pending, to aid in treating or disposing of it;

**47.** `[C0699 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: the adoption of one of them always does _____ this other motion—that is, changes its status in some way—without adopting or expressly rejecting it.
   A. approve
   B. by paragraph or
   C. something to
   D. general order

   *Answer:* C) something to. See RONR (12th ed.) 6:6 — “the adoption of one of them always does something to this other motion—that is, changes its status in some way—without adopting or expressly rejecting it.”

**48.** `[C0724 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): From these rules, it follows that the motion to _____ can be applied to any of the four subsidiary motions of lower rank (but not to the two that rank above it), while the _____ can be applied to any of the five subsidiary motions that rank below it (but not to the one subsidiary motion that ranks above it).

   *Answer:* Limit or Extend Limits of Debate, Previous Question — “From these rules, it follows that the motion to Limit or Extend Limits of Debate can be applied to any of the four subsidiary motions of lower rank (but not to the two that rank above it), while the Previous Question can be applied to any of the five subsidiary motions that rank below it (but not to the one subsidiary motion that ranks above it).”. See RONR (12th ed.) 6:8 — “From these rules, it follows that the motion to Limit or Extend Limits of Debate can be applied to any of the four subsidiary motions of lower rank (but not to the two that rank above it), while the Previous Question can be applied to any of the five subsidiary motions that rank below it (but not to the one subsidiary motion that ranks above it).”

**49.** `[C0724 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: The four lowest-ranking subsidiary motions can be debated (except that _____ is undebatable when it is applied to an undebatable motion).
   A. Adopted
   B. meeting
   C. Amend
   D. Time

   *Answer:* C) Amend. See RONR (12th ed.) 6:8 — “The four lowest-ranking subsidiary motions can be debated (except that Amend is undebatable when it is applied to an undebatable motion).”

**50.** `[C0779 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): If previous notice is given _____, it can be given orally unless the rules of the organization require it to be in writing—which is often the case with notice of amendments to bylaws.

   *Answer:* at a meeting — “If previous notice is given at a meeting, it can be given orally unless the rules of the organization require it to be in writing—which is often the case with notice of amendments to bylaws.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:47 — “If previous notice is given at a meeting, it can be given orally unless the rules of the organization require it to be in writing—which is often the case with notice of amendments to bylaws.”

**51.** `[C0779 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: If previous notice is given _____, it can be given orally unless the rules of the organization require it to be in writing—which is often the case with notice of amendments to bylaws.
   A. extend the limits
   B. at a meeting
   C. Motions Relating to Methods of Voting,
   D. show of hands

   *Answer:* B) at a meeting. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:47 — “If previous notice is given at a meeting, it can be given orally unless the rules of the organization require it to be in writing—which is often the case with notice of amendments to bylaws.”

**52.** `[C0886 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): When the _____ Question (16) is ordered on the resolution before the preamble has been considered for amendment, however, the _____ does not apply to the preamble, which becomes open to debate and amendment unless the Previous Question is then separately ordered on it also.

   *Answer:* Previous, Previous Question — “When the Previous Question (16) is ordered on the resolution before the preamble has been considered for amendment, however, the Previous Question does not apply to the preamble, which becomes open to debate and amendment unless the Previous Question is then separately ordered on it also.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:19 — “When the Previous Question (16) is ordered on the resolution before the preamble has been considered for amendment, however, the Previous Question does not apply to the preamble, which becomes open to debate and amendment unless the Previous Question is then separately ordered on it also.”

**53.** `[C0886 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: When the Previous _____ (16) is ordered on the resolution before the preamble has been considered for amendment, however, the Previous Question does not apply to the preamble, which becomes open to debate and amendment unless the Previous Question is then separately ordered on it also.
   A. Information
   B. scribe
   C. Question
   D. bylaws

   *Answer:* C) Question. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:19 — “When the Previous Question (16) is ordered on the resolution before the preamble has been considered for amendment, however, the Previous Question does not apply to the preamble, which becomes open to debate and amendment unless the Previous Question is then separately ordered on it also.”

**54.** `[C0900 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): Similarly, “A _____ takes precedence over any pending question (of no matter how high a rank) out of which it arises”—but it does so only at the time the breach of order occurs.

   *Answer:* Point of Order — “Similarly, “A Point of Order takes precedence over any pending question (of no matter how high a rank) out of which it arises”—but it does so only at the time the breach of order occurs.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 6:20 — “Similarly, “A Point of Order takes precedence over any pending question (of no matter how high a rank) out of which it arises”—but it does so only at the time the breach of order occurs.”

**55.** `[C0900 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: but an Objection to the Consideration of a Question is legitimate only against an _____ main motion, and the objection is no longer in order after consideration of the question has begun—even though an original main motion is immediately pending (26).
   A. original
   B. class
   C. Raise a Question of
   D. first paragraph

   *Answer:* A) original. See RONR (12th ed.) 6:20 — “but an Objection to the Consideration of a Question is legitimate only against an original main motion, and the objection is no longer in order after consideration of the question has begun—even though an original main motion is immediately pending (26).”

**56.** `[C0975 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): Below for the main motion, and in each of the succeeding sections covering the different motions of parliamentary law (11–37), is a subsection headed _____ giving a script showing the words to be spoken by a member making the motion and by the chair in stating and putting the question on it.

   *Answer:* Form and Example — “Below for the main motion, and in each of the succeeding sections covering the different motions of parliamentary law (11–37), is a subsection headed Form and Example giving a script showing the words to be spoken by a member making the motion and by the chair in stating and putting the question on it.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:37 — “Below for the main motion, and in each of the succeeding sections covering the different motions of parliamentary law (11–37), is a subsection headed Form and Example giving a script showing the words to be spoken by a member making the motion and by the chair in stating and putting the question on it.”

**57.** `[C0975 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: Below for the main motion, and in each of the succeeding sections covering the different motions of parliamentary law (11–37), is a subsection headed _____ giving a script showing the words to be spoken by a member making the motion and by the chair in stating and putting the question on it.
   A. opinion
   B. mass meeting
   C. Form and Example
   D. viva voce

   *Answer:* C) Form and Example. See RONR (12th ed.) 10:37 — “Below for the main motion, and in each of the succeeding sections covering the different motions of parliamentary law (11–37), is a subsection headed Form and Example giving a script showing the words to be spoken by a member making the motion and by the chair in stating and putting the question on it.”

**58.** `[C0977 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): In such a case, motions to _____ _____, for the Previous Question, and to Lay on the Table are in order;

   *Answer:* Extend Limits of Debate, Limit or — “In such a case, motions to Limit or Extend Limits of Debate, for the Previous Question, and to Lay on the Table are in order;”. See RONR (12th ed.) 6:7 — “In such a case, motions to Limit or Extend Limits of Debate, for the Previous Question, and to Lay on the Table are in order;”

**59.** `[C0977 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: motions to Postpone Indefinitely, to Amend, and to Commit, on the other hand, may have become pending before the motion to _____ was moved, but none of these three motions can now be made—except that it is in order to move to amend the motion to Postpone, while it is immediately pending.
   A. Division of the
   B. Postpone Definitely
   C. Robert’s Rules
   D. of the board

   *Answer:* B) Postpone Definitely. See RONR (12th ed.) 6:7 — “motions to Postpone Indefinitely, to Amend, and to Commit, on the other hand, may have become pending before the motion to Postpone Definitely was moved, but none of these three motions can now be made—except that it is in order to move to amend the motion to Postpone, while it is immediately pending.”

**60.** `[C1072 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): For example, a _____ (2) can be suspended for the duration of a session (8);

   *Answer:* standing rule — “For example, a standing rule (2) can be suspended for the duration of a session (8);”. See RONR (12th ed.) 6:23 — “For example, a standing rule (2) can be suspended for the duration of a session (8);”

**61.** `[C1072 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: For example, a _____ (2) can be suspended for the duration of a session (8);
   A. standing rule
   B. ballot
   C. Unfinished Business and General Orders
   D. ad hoc

   *Answer:* A) standing rule. See RONR (12th ed.) 6:23 — “For example, a standing rule (2) can be suspended for the duration of a session (8);”

---

## Domain 2: Subsidiary and Privileged Motions

**1.** `[K0197 · Order of precedence (ranking)]` Which of these motions has the highest precedence (is taken up first)?
   A. Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn
   B. Previous Question
   C. Amend
   D. Recess

   *Answer:* Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn. See RONR (12th ed.) 22:1 — “The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.”

**2.** `[K0134 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Recess → Lay on the Table → Amend → Postpone Indefinitely. See RONR (12th ed.) 20:1 — “A recess is a short intermission in the assembly’s proceedings, commonly of only a few minutes, which does not close the meeting and after which business will immediately be resumed at exactly the point where it was interrupted.”

**3.** `[K0215 · Order of precedence (ranking)]` Which of these motions has the highest precedence (is taken up first)?
   A. Amend
   B. Postpone to a Certain Time
   C. Lay on the Table

   *Answer:* Lay on the Table. See RONR (12th ed.) 17:1 — “The motion to Lay on the Table enables the assembly to lay the pending question aside temporarily when something else of immediate urgency has arisen or when something else needs to be addressed before consideration of the pending question is resumed, in such a way that:”

**4.** `[K0012 · Amendability]` Can the motion to Recess be amended?
   A. Amendable
   B. Not amendable

   *Answer:* Amendable. See RONR (12th ed.) 20:1 — “A recess is a short intermission in the assembly’s proceedings, commonly of only a few minutes, which does not close the meeting and after which business will immediately be resumed at exactly the point where it was interrupted.”

**5.** `[K0207 · Order of precedence (ranking)]` Which of these motions has the highest precedence (is taken up first)?
   A. Postpone Indefinitely
   B. Adjourn
   C. Lay on the Table

   *Answer:* Adjourn. See RONR (12th ed.) 21:1 — “A motion to adjourn may be a privileged or a main motion depending on a number of conditions.”

**6.** `[K0154 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Adjourn → Raise a Question of Privilege → Previous Question → Postpone to a Certain Time. See RONR (12th ed.) 21:1 — “A motion to adjourn may be a privileged or a main motion depending on a number of conditions.”

**7.** `[K0027 · Second required]` Does the motion to Previous Question require a second?
   A. Requires a second
   B. No second required

   *Answer:* Requires a second. See RONR (12th ed.) 16:1 — “The Previous Question is the motion used to bring the assembly to an immediate vote on one or more pending questions; its adoption does this with certain exceptions.”

**8.** `[K0032 · Amendability]` Can the motion to Limit or Extend Limits of Debate be amended?
   A. Amendable
   B. Not amendable

   *Answer:* Amendable. See RONR (12th ed.) 15:1 — “The subsidiary motion to Limit or Extend Limits of Debate is one of the two motions by means of which an assembly can exercise special control over debate on a pending question or on a series of pending questions.”

**9.** `[K0114 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn → Recess → Raise a Question of Privilege → Commit or Refer. See RONR (12th ed.) 22:1 — “The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.”

**10.** `[K0017 · Vote required]` What vote does the motion to Call for the Orders of the Day require to be adopted?
   A. Majority vote
   B. Two-thirds vote
   C. No vote (chair rules / demand)
   D. Unanimous consent

   *Answer:* No vote (chair rules / demand). See RONR (12th ed.) 18:1 — “A Call for the Orders of the Day is a privileged motion by which a member can require the assembly to conform to its agenda, program, or order of business, or to take up a general or special order that is due to come up at the time (14, 41), unless two thirds of those voting wish to do otherwise.”

**11.** `[K0089 · Order of precedence (ranking)]` Which of these motions has the highest precedence (is taken up first)?
   A. Postpone to a Certain Time
   B. Commit or Refer
   C. Amend

   *Answer:* Postpone to a Certain Time. See RONR (12th ed.) 14:1 — “The subsidiary motion to Postpone to a Certain Time (or Postpone Definitely, or Postpone) is the motion by which action on a pending question can be put off, within limits, to a definite session, day, meeting, or hour, or until after a certain event.”

**12.** `[K0155 · Order of precedence (ranking)]` Which of these motions has the highest precedence (is taken up first)?
   A. Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn
   B. Postpone Indefinitely
   C. Limit or Extend Limits of Debate

   *Answer:* Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn. See RONR (12th ed.) 22:1 — “The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.”

   *Answer:* Recess → Raise a Question of Privilege → Call for the Orders of the Day. See RONR (12th ed.) 20:1 — “A recess is a short intermission in the assembly’s proceedings, commonly of only a few minutes, which does not close the meeting and after which business will immediately be resumed at exactly the point where it was interrupted.”

**42.** `[K0210 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn → Lay on the Table → Postpone to a Certain Time → Amend. See RONR (12th ed.) 22:1 — “The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.”

**43.** `[K0269 · Order of precedence (ranking)]` Which of these motions has the highest precedence (is taken up first)?
   A. Commit or Refer
   B. Previous Question
   C. Lay on the Table
   D. Adjourn

   *Answer:* Adjourn. See RONR (12th ed.) 21:1 — “A motion to adjourn may be a privileged or a main motion depending on a number of conditions.”

**44.** `[K0084 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Lay on the Table → Previous Question → Limit or Extend Limits of Debate. See RONR (12th ed.) 17:1 — “The motion to Lay on the Table enables the assembly to lay the pending question aside temporarily when something else of immediate urgency has arisen or when something else needs to be addressed before consideration of the pending question is resumed, in such a way that:”

   *Answer:* Adjourn → Recess → Raise a Question of Privilege. See RONR (12th ed.) 21:1 — “A motion to adjourn may be a privileged or a main motion depending on a number of conditions.”

See RONR (12th ed.) 20:1 — “A recess is a short intermission in the assembly’s proceedings, commonly of only a few minutes, which does not close the meeting and after which business will immediately be resumed at exactly the point where it was interrupted.”

**49.** `[K0035 · Second required]` Does the motion to Postpone to a Certain Time require a second?
   A. Requires a second
   B. No second required

   *Answer:* Requires a second. See RONR (12th ed.) 14:1 — “The subsidiary motion to Postpone to a Certain Time (or Postpone Definitely, or Postpone) is the motion by which action on a pending question can be put off, within limits, to a definite session, day, meeting, or hour, or until after a certain event.”

**64.** `[K0001 · Vote required]` What vote does the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn require to be adopted?
   A. Majority vote
   B. Two-thirds vote
   C. No vote (chair rules / demand)
   D. Unanimous consent

   *Answer:* Majority vote. See RONR (12th ed.) 22:1 — “The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.”

**65.** `[K0137 · Order of precedence (ranking)]` Which of these motions has the highest precedence (is taken up first)?
   A. Limit or Extend Limits of Debate
   B. Postpone to a Certain Time
   C. Commit or Refer
   D. Call for the Orders of the Day

   *Answer:* Call for the Orders of the Day. See RONR (12th ed.) 18:1 — “A Call for the Orders of the Day is a privileged motion by which a member can require the assembly to conform to its agenda, program, or order of business, or to take up a general or special order that is due to come up at the time (14, 41), unless two thirds of those voting wish to do otherwise.”

**66.** `[K0041 · Vote required]` What vote does the motion to Amend require to be adopted?
   A. Majority vote
   B. Two-thirds vote
   C. No vote (chair rules / demand)
   D. Unanimous consent

   *Answer:* Majority vote. See RONR (12th ed.) 12:1 — “The subsidiary motion to Amend is a motion to modify the wording—and within certain limits the meaning—of a pending motion before the pending motion itself is acted upon.”

   *Answer:* Commit or Refer. **103.** `[K0092 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Commit or Refer → Amend → Postpone Indefinitely. See RONR (12th ed.) 13:1 — “The subsidiary motion to Commit or Refer is generally used to send a pending question to a relatively small group of selected persons—a committee—so that the question may be carefully investigated and put into better condition for the assembly to consider.”

**104.** `[K0267 · Order of precedence (ranking)]` Which of these motions has the highest precedence (is taken up first)?
   A. Postpone to a Certain Time
   B. Limit or Extend Limits of Debate
   C. Commit or Refer

   *Answer:* Limit or Extend Limits of Debate. See RONR (12th ed.) 15:1 — “The subsidiary motion to Limit or Extend Limits of Debate is one of the two motions by means of which an assembly can exercise special control over debate on a pending question or on a series of pending questions.”

**105.** `[K0129 · Order of precedence (ranking)]` Which of these motions has the highest precedence (is taken up first)?
   A. Adjourn
   B. Call for the Orders of the Day
   C. Postpone Indefinitely
   D. Raise a Question of Privilege

   *Answer:* Adjourn. See RONR (12th ed.) 21:1 — “A motion to adjourn may be a privileged or a main motion depending on a number of conditions.”

**106.** `[K0037 · Vote required]` What vote does the motion to Commit or Refer require to be adopted?
   A. Majority vote
   B. Two-thirds vote
   C. No vote (chair rules / demand)
   D. Unanimous consent

   *Answer:* Majority vote. See RONR (12th ed.) 13:1 — “The subsidiary motion to Commit or Refer is generally used to send a pending question to a relatively small group of selected persons—a committee—so that the question may be carefully investigated and put into better condition for the assembly to consider.”

**107.** `[K0040 · Amendability]` Can the motion to Commit or Refer be amended?
   A. Amendable
   B. Not amendable

   *Answer:* Amendable. See RONR (12th ed.) 13:1 — “The subsidiary motion to Commit or Refer is generally used to send a pending question to a relatively small group of selected persons—a committee—so that the question may be carefully investigated and put into better condition for the assembly to consider.”

**108.** `[K0122 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn → Call for the Orders of the Day → Limit or Extend Limits of Debate → Amend. See RONR (12th ed.) 22:1 — “The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.”

**109.** `[K0202 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Adjourn → Call for the Orders of the Day → Previous Question → Amend. See RONR (12th ed.) 21:1 — “A motion to adjourn may be a privileged or a main motion depending on a number of conditions.”

**110.** `[K0200 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Recess → Postpone to a Certain Time → Postpone Indefinitely. See RONR (12th ed.) 20:1 — “A recess is a short intermission in the assembly’s proceedings, commonly of only a few minutes, which does not close the meeting and after which business will immediately be resumed at exactly the point where it was interrupted.”

**111.** `[K0205 · Order of precedence (ranking)]` Which of these motions has the highest precedence (is taken up first)?
   A. Recess
   B. Call for the Orders of the Day
   C. Limit or Extend Limits of Debate
   D. Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn

   *Answer:* Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn. See RONR (12th ed.) 22:1 — “The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.”

   C. Previous Question

   *Answer:* Lay on the Table. See RONR (12th ed.) 17:1 — “The motion to Lay on the Table enables the assembly to lay the pending question aside temporarily when something else of immediate urgency has arisen or when something else needs to be addressed before consideration of the pending question is resumed, in such a way that:”

**117.** `[K0232 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Adjourn → Recess → Commit or Refer. See RONR (12th ed.) 21:1 — “A motion to adjourn may be a privileged or a main motion depending on a number of conditions.”

**118.** `[K0043 · Second required]` Does the motion to Amend require a second?
   A. Requires a second
   B. No second required

   *Answer:* Requires a second. See RONR (12th ed.) 12:1 — “The subsidiary motion to Amend is a motion to modify the wording—and within certain limits the meaning—of a pending motion before the pending motion itself is acted upon.”

**119.** `[K0174 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Adjourn → Previous Question → Postpone to a Certain Time → Commit or Refer. See RONR (12th ed.) 21:1 — “A motion to adjourn may be a privileged or a main motion depending on a number of conditions.”

**120.** `[K0110 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Postpone to a Certain Time → Commit or Refer → Amend → Postpone Indefinitely. See RONR (12th ed.) 14:1 — “The subsidiary motion to Postpone to a Certain Time (or Postpone Definitely, or Postpone) is the motion by which action on a pending question can be put off, within limits, to a definite session, day, meeting, or hour, or until after a certain event.”

**124.** `[K0013 · Vote required]` What vote does the motion to Raise a Question of Privilege require to be adopted?
   A. Majority vote
   B. Two-thirds vote
   C. No vote (chair rules / demand)
   D. Unanimous consent

   *Answer:* No vote (chair rules / demand). See RONR (12th ed.) 19:1 — “To Raise a Question of Privilege is a device that permits a request or main motion relating to the rights and privileges of the assembly or any of its members to be brought up for possible immediate consideration because of its urgency, while business is pending and the request or motion would…”

**125.** `[K0176 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Call for the Orders of the Day → Postpone to a Certain Time → Postpone Indefinitely. See RONR (12th ed.) 18:1 — “A Call for the Orders of the Day is a privileged motion by which a member can require the assembly to conform to its agenda, program, or order of business, or to take up a general or special order that is due to come up at the time (14, 41), unless two thirds of those voting wish to do otherwise.”

**167.** `[K0093 · Order of precedence (ranking)]` Which of these motions has the highest precedence (is taken up first)?
   A. Recess
   B. Adjourn
   C. Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn
   D. Raise a Question of Privilege

   *Answer:* Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn. See RONR (12th ed.) 22:1 — “The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.”

**168.** `[K0218 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn → Raise a Question of Privilege → Call for the Orders of the Day → Limit or Extend Limits of Debate. See RONR (12th ed.) 22:1 — “The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.”

**169.** `[K0158 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Adjourn → Lay on the Table → Limit or Extend Limits of Debate → Commit or Refer. See RONR (12th ed.) 21:1 — “A motion to adjourn may be a privileged or a main motion depending on a number of conditions.”

**170.** `[K0102 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Call for the Orders of the Day → Lay on the Table → Previous Question → Limit or Extend Limits of Debate. See RONR (12th ed.) 18:1 — “A Call for the Orders of the Day is a privileged motion by which a member can require the assembly to conform to its agenda, program, or order of business, or to take up a general or special order that is due to come up at the time (14, 41), unless two thirds of those voting wish to do otherwise.”

   B. No second required

   *Answer:* Requires a second. See RONR (12th ed.) 17:1 — “The motion to Lay on the Table enables the assembly to lay the pending question aside temporarily when something else of immediate urgency has arisen or when something else needs to be addressed before consideration of the pending question is resumed, in such a way that:”

See RONR (12th ed.) 22:1 — “The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.”

**229.** `[K0042 · Debatability]` Is the motion to Amend debatable?
   A. Debatable
   B. Not debatable

   *Answer:* Debatable. See RONR (12th ed.) 12:1 — “The subsidiary motion to Amend is a motion to modify the wording—and within certain limits the meaning—of a pending motion before the pending motion itself is acted upon.”

**230.** `[K0021 · Vote required]` What vote does the motion to Lay on the Table require to be adopted?
   A. Majority vote
   B. Two-thirds vote
   C. No vote (chair rules / demand)
   D. Unanimous consent

   *Answer:* Majority vote. See RONR (12th ed.) 17:1 — “The motion to Lay on the Table enables the assembly to lay the pending question aside temporarily when something else of immediate urgency has arisen or when something else needs to be addressed before consideration of the pending question is resumed, in such a way that:”

**231.** `[K0105 · Order of precedence (ranking)]` Which of these motions has the highest precedence (is taken up first)?
   A. Postpone to a Certain Time
   B. Commit or Refer
   C. Previous Question
   D. Limit or Extend Limits of Debate

   *Answer:* Previous Question. See RONR (12th ed.) 16:1 — “The Previous Question is the motion used to bring the assembly to an immediate vote on one or more pending questions; its adoption does this with certain exceptions.”

**234.** `[K0138 · Order of precedence (ordering)]` Tap these motions in order of precedence, highest first.

   *Answer:* Call for the Orders of the Day → Limit or Extend Limits of Debate → Postpone to a Certain Time → Commit or Refer. See RONR (12th ed.) 18:1 — “A Call for the Orders of the Day is a privileged motion by which a member can require the assembly to conform to its agenda, program, or order of business, or to take up a general or special order that is due to come up at the time (14, 41), unless two thirds of those voting wish to do otherwise.”

**244.** `[K0039 · Second required]` Does the motion to Commit or Refer require a second?

   B. No second required

   *Answer:* Requires a second.    C. Reconsider,
   D. parliamentary law

   *Answer:* A) primary. See RONR (12th ed.) 12:42 — “It should be noted that in the preceding example the chair gives the primary amendment as it would read if the secondary amendment were adopted.”

**327.** `[C0358 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The object of the motion to _____ (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.

   *Answer:* Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn — “The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.”. **328.** `[C0358 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: The object of the motion to _____ (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.
   A. Platform Committee
   B. Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn
   C. Discharge a Committee
   D. censure

   *Answer:* B) Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn. See RONR (12th ed.) 22:1 — “The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn.”

   *Answer:* substitute, substitute — “A motion to Amend by striking out an entire paragraph, section, or article—or a complete main motion or resolution—and inserting a different paragraph or other unit in its place is called a motion to substitute, and the paragraph or resolution to be inserted is said to be offered (or proposed) as “a substitute.” A substitute can be offered for a paragraph or a main motion of only one sentence, and in such a case the paragraph proposed as a substitute can contain several sentences.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 12:69 — “A motion to Amend by striking out an entire paragraph, section, or article—or a complete main motion or resolution—and inserting a different paragraph or other unit in its place is called a motion to substitute, and the paragraph or resolution to be inserted is said to be offered (or proposed) as “a substitute.” A substitute can be offered for a paragraph or a main motion of only one sentence, and in such a case the paragraph proposed as a substitute can contain several sentences.”

**375.** `[C0621 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): By these rules, if a proposed amendment is related to the main motion in such a way that, after the adoption, rejection, or temporary disposal of the present main motion, the essential idea of the amendment could _____ be introduced as an independent resolution during the same session, the amendment is germane and must be admitted, since there will not, or may not, be any opportunity to present it later.

   *Answer:* not — “By these rules, if a proposed amendment is related to the main motion in such a way that, after the adoption, rejection, or temporary disposal of the present main motion, the essential idea of the amendment could not be introduced as an independent resolution during the same session, the amendment is germane and must be admitted, since there will not, or may not, be any opportunity to present it later.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 12:18 — “By these rules, if a proposed amendment is related to the main motion in such a way that, after the adoption, rejection, or temporary disposal of the present main motion, the essential idea of the amendment could not be introduced as an independent resolution during the same session, the amendment is germane and must be admitted, since there will not, or may not, be any opportunity to present it later.”

   *Answer:* C) primary amendment. **423.** `[C0851 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): Sometimes the mere making of a motion for the _____ or “call for the question” may motivate unanimous consent to ending debate.

   *Answer:* Previous Question, Question — “Sometimes the mere making of a motion for the Previous Question or “call for the question” may motivate unanimous consent to ending debate.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 16:7 — “Sometimes the mere making of a motion for the Previous Question or “call for the question” may motivate unanimous consent to ending debate.”

   *Answer:* B) Previous. See RONR (12th ed.) 16:7 — “Sometimes the mere making of a motion for the Previous Question or “call for the question” may motivate unanimous consent to ending debate.”

**427.** `[C0858 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): Even if the entire resolution or main motion is replaced, adopting the motion to substitute only _____ the resolution, which remains pending as amended.

   *Answer:* amends — “Even if the entire resolution or main motion is replaced, adopting the motion to substitute only amends the resolution, which remains pending as amended.”. **428.** `[C0858 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: In taking the vote on whether to make the substitution, the chair should first read both the paragraph of the original text and the proposed _____—as they stand at the time as amended.

   D. Standard

   *Answer:* B) substitute. See RONR (12th ed.) 12:73 — “In taking the vote on whether to make the substitution, the chair should first read both the paragraph of the original text and the proposed substitute—as they stand at the time as amended.”

**429.** `[C0865 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): If the effect would be to change action already taken by the assembly, as, for example, “to postpone for three weeks the dinner scheduled for October 15,” such a motion is a particular case of the motion to _____ _____ (35).

   *Answer:* Something Previously Adopted, Amend — “If the effect would be to change action already taken by the assembly, as, for example, “to postpone for three weeks the dinner scheduled for October 15,” such a motion is a particular case of the motion to Amend Something Previously Adopted (35).”. ---

## Domain 3: Incidental Motions and Motions that Bring a Question Again Before the Assembly

**1.** `[K0070 · Debatability]` Is the motion to Division of the Assembly debatable?
   A. Debatable
   B. Not debatable

   *Answer:* Not debatable. See RONR (12th ed.) 29:1 — “Whenever a member doubts the result of a voice (vivavoce) vote or a vote by show of hands—either because the result appears close or because he doubts that a representative number of the members present have voted— he can call for a Division of the Assembly, thereby requiring the vote to be taken…”

**2.** `[K0064 · Amendability]` Can the motion to Suspend the Rules be amended?
   A. Amendable
   B. Not amendable

   *Answer:* Not amendable. See RONR (12th ed.) 25:1 — “When an assembly wishes to do something during a meeting that it cannot do without violating one or more of its regular rules, it can adopt a motion to Suspend the Rules interfering with the proposed action—provided that the proposal is not in conflict with the organization’s bylaws (or…”

**3.** `[K0063 · Second required]` Does the motion to Suspend the Rules require a second?
   A. Requires a second
   B. No second required

   *Answer:* Requires a second. See RONR (12th ed.) 25:1 — “When an assembly wishes to do something during a meeting that it cannot do without violating one or more of its regular rules, it can adopt a motion to Suspend the Rules interfering with the proposed action—provided that the proposal is not in conflict with the organization’s bylaws (or…”

**4.** `[K0067 · Second required]` Does the motion to Object to the Consideration of a Question require a second?
   A. Requires a second
   B. No second required

   *Answer:* No second required. See RONR (12th ed.) 26:1 — “The purpose of an Objection to the Consideration of a Question is to enable the assembly to avoid a particular original main motion altogether when it believes it would be strongly undesirable for the motion even to come before the assembly.”

**5.** `[K0065 · Vote required]` What vote does the motion to Object to the Consideration of a Question require to be adopted?
   A. Majority vote
   B. Two-thirds vote
   C. No vote (chair rules / demand)
   D. Unanimous consent

   *Answer:* Two-thirds vote. See RONR (12th ed.) 26:1 — “The purpose of an Objection to the Consideration of a Question is to enable the assembly to avoid a particular original main motion altogether when it believes it would be strongly undesirable for the motion even to come before the assembly.”

**6.** `[K0053 · Vote required]` What vote does the motion to Point of Order require to be adopted?
   A. Majority vote
   B. Two-thirds vote
   C. No vote (chair rules / demand)
   D. Unanimous consent

   *Answer:* No vote (chair rules / demand). See RONR (12th ed.) 23:1 — “When a member thinks that the rules of the assembly are being violated, he can make a Point of Order (or “raise a question of order,” as it is sometimes expressed), thereby calling upon the chair for a ruling and an enforcement of the regular rules.”

**7.** `[K0062 · Debatability]` Is the motion to Suspend the Rules debatable?
   A. Debatable
   B. Not debatable

   *Answer:* Not debatable. See RONR (12th ed.) 25:1 — “When an assembly wishes to do something during a meeting that it cannot do without violating one or more of its regular rules, it can adopt a motion to Suspend the Rules interfering with the proposed action—provided that the proposal is not in conflict with the organization’s bylaws (or…”

**8.** `[K0068 · Amendability]` Can the motion to Object to the Consideration of a Question be amended?
   A. Amendable
   B. Not amendable

   *Answer:* Not amendable. See RONR (12th ed.) 26:1 — “The purpose of an Objection to the Consideration of a Question is to enable the assembly to avoid a particular original main motion altogether when it believes it would be strongly undesirable for the motion even to come before the assembly.”

**9.** `[K0058 · Debatability]` Is the motion to Appeal debatable?
   A. Debatable
   B. Not debatable

   *Answer:* Debatable. See RONR (12th ed.) 24:1 — “By electing a presiding officer, the assembly delegates to him the authority and duty to make necessary rulings on questions of parliamentary law.”

**10.** `[K0061 · Vote required]` What vote does the motion to Suspend the Rules require to be adopted?

   *Answer:* Two-thirds vote. See RONR (12th ed.) 25:1 — “When an assembly wishes to do something during a meeting that it cannot do without violating one or more of its regular rules, it can adopt a motion to Suspend the Rules interfering with the proposed action—provided that the proposal is not in conflict with the organization’s bylaws (or…”

   B. Not amendable

**110.** `[C0684 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): When a motion relating to a single subject contains several parts, each of which is capable of standing as a complete proposition if the others are removed, the parts can be separated to be considered and voted on as if they were distinct questions—by adoption of the motion for _____ _____ (or “to divide the question”).

   *Answer:* Division of a, Question — “When a motion relating to a single subject contains several parts, each of which is capable of standing as a complete proposition if the others are removed, the parts can be separated to be considered and voted on as if they were distinct questions—by adoption of the motion for Division of a Question (or “to divide the question”).”. See RONR (12th ed.) 27:1 — “When a motion relating to a single subject contains several parts, each of which is capable of standing as a complete proposition if the others are removed, the parts can be separated to be considered and voted on as if they were distinct questions—by adoption of the motion for Division of a Question (or “to divide the question”).”

**161.** `[C1104 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): If it is desired to reconsider the secondary amendment after the main question has been finally disposed of, the secondary amendment, the primary amendment, and the main question must all be reconsidered, and one motion to _____ should be made covering the votes of these three motions.

   *Answer:* Reconsider — “If it is desired to reconsider the secondary amendment after the main question has been finally disposed of, the secondary amendment, the primary amendment, and the main question must all be reconsidered, and one motion to Reconsider should be made covering the votes of these three motions.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 37:31 — “If it is desired to reconsider the secondary amendment after the main question has been finally disposed of, the secondary amendment, the primary amendment, and the main question must all be reconsidered, and one motion to Reconsider should be made covering the votes of these three motions.”

**162.** `[C1104 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: If it is desired to reconsider the secondary amendment after the main question has been finally disposed of, the secondary amendment, the primary amendment, and the main question must all be reconsidered, and one motion to _____ should be made covering the votes of these three motions.
   A. house of
   B. Form and
   C. commend
   D. Reconsider

   *Answer:* D) Reconsider. See RONR (12th ed.) 37:31 — “If it is desired to reconsider the secondary amendment after the main question has been finally disposed of, the secondary amendment, the primary amendment, and the main question must all be reconsidered, and one motion to Reconsider should be made covering the votes of these three motions.”

## Domain 4: Organization and Conduct of Meetings

**1.** `[C0004 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): It formerly was common practice to divide the basic rules of an organization into two documents, in order that one of them —the _____—might be made more difficult to amend than the other, to which the name _____ was applied.

   *Answer:* constitution, bylaws — “It formerly was common practice to divide the basic rules of an organization into two documents, in order that one of them —the constitution—might be made more difficult to amend than the other, to which the name bylaws was applied.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 2:10 — “It formerly was common practice to divide the basic rules of an organization into two documents, in order that one of them —the constitution—might be made more difficult to amend than the other, to which the name bylaws was applied.”

**2.** `[C0004 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: It formerly was common practice to divide the basic rules of an organization into two documents, in order that one of them —the _____—might be made more difficult to amend than the other, to which the name bylaws was applied.
   A. settlement
   B. one fifth of
   C. constitution
   D. bylaws

   *Answer:* C) constitution. See RONR (12th ed.) 2:10 — “It formerly was common practice to divide the basic rules of an organization into two documents, in order that one of them —the constitution—might be made more difficult to amend than the other, to which the name bylaws was applied.”

**3.** `[C0010 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): Meetings of permanently organized bodies usually follow an established _____ that specifies the sequence in which certain general types or classes of business are to be brought up or permitted to be introduced.

   *Answer:* order of business — “Meetings of permanently organized bodies usually follow an established order of business that specifies the sequence in which certain general types or classes of business are to be brought up or permitted to be introduced.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 3:16 — “Meetings of permanently organized bodies usually follow an established order of business that specifies the sequence in which certain general types or classes of business are to be brought up or permitted to be introduced.”

**4.** `[C0010 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: Meetings of permanently organized bodies usually follow an established _____ that specifies the sequence in which certain general types or classes of business are to be brought up or permitted to be introduced.
   A. sustaining
   B. except
   C. quorum
   D. order of business

   *Answer:* D) order of business. See RONR (12th ed.) 3:16 — “Meetings of permanently organized bodies usually follow an established order of business that specifies the sequence in which certain general types or classes of business are to be brought up or permitted to be introduced.”

**5.** `[C0015 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): When a decision is to be based on more than a _____, the requirement most commonly specified is a _____— that is, the expressed approval of at least two thirds of those present and voting.

   *Answer:* majority, two-thirds vote — “When a decision is to be based on more than a majority, the requirement most commonly specified is a two-thirds vote— that is, the expressed approval of at least two thirds of those present and voting.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 1:7 — “When a decision is to be based on more than a majority, the requirement most commonly specified is a two-thirds vote— that is, the expressed approval of at least two thirds of those present and voting.”

**6.** `[C0015 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: When a decision is to be based on more than a majority, the requirement most commonly specified is a _____— that is, the expressed approval of at least two thirds of those present and voting.
   A. finally, disposed of
   B. two-thirds vote
   C. Order
   D. Unfinished Business and General Orders

   *Answer:* B) two-thirds vote. See RONR (12th ed.) 1:7 — “When a decision is to be based on more than a majority, the requirement most commonly specified is a two-thirds vote— that is, the expressed approval of at least two thirds of those present and voting.”

**7.** `[C0018 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The minimum number of members who must be present at the meetings of a deliberative assembly for business to be validly transacted is the _____ of the assembly.

   *Answer:* quorum — “The minimum number of members who must be present at the meetings of a deliberative assembly for business to be validly transacted is the quorum of the assembly.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 3:3 — “The minimum number of members who must be present at the meetings of a deliberative assembly for business to be validly transacted is the quorum of the assembly.”

**8.** `[C0018 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: The minimum number of members who must be present at the meetings of a deliberative assembly for business to be validly transacted is the _____ of the assembly.
   A. Suspend
   B. quorum
   C. speed up
   D. bylaws

   *Answer:* B) quorum. See RONR (12th ed.) 3:3 — “The minimum number of members who must be present at the meetings of a deliberative assembly for business to be validly transacted is the quorum of the assembly.”

**9.** `[C0064 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): A _____ (as explained under _____ below) is any question which, usually by postponement, has been made an order of the day without being made a special order.

   *Answer:* general order, Orders of the Day, — “A general order (as explained under Orders of the Day, below) is any question which, usually by postponement, has been made an order of the day without being made a special order.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 41:22 — “A general order (as explained under Orders of the Day, below) is any question which, usually by postponement, has been made an order of the day without being made a special order.”

**10.** `[C0064 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: A _____ (as explained under Orders of the Day, below) is any question which, usually by postponement, has been made an order of the day without being made a special order.
   A. Postpone Indefinitely
   B. general order
   C. hearing
   D. session

   *Answer:* B) general order. See RONR (12th ed.) 41:22 — “A general order (as explained under Orders of the Day, below) is any question which, usually by postponement, has been made an order of the day without being made a special order.”

**11.** `[C0065 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): for example, although a member may have begun by debating a pending motion, he may conclude by moving any secondary motion, including the _____ (16), that is in order at the time.

   *Answer:* Previous Question — “for example, although a member may have begun by debating a pending motion, he may conclude by moving any secondary motion, including the Previous Question (16), that is in order at the time.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 42:5 — “for example, although a member may have begun by debating a pending motion, he may conclude by moving any secondary motion, including the Previous Question (16), that is in order at the time.”

**12.** `[C0065 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: for example, although a member may have begun by debating a pending motion, he may conclude by moving any secondary motion, including the _____ (16), that is in order at the time.

   B. in good standing

   *Answer:* C) Previous Question. See RONR (12th ed.) 42:5 — “for example, although a member may have begun by debating a pending motion, he may conclude by moving any secondary motion, including the Previous Question (16), that is in order at the time.”

**13.** `[C0066 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): Such exceptions occur only through one of the processes by which, from one session to another, a main motion can remain within the control of the assembly (that is, _____ _____), so that the same motion can be considered at the later session.

   *Answer:* temporarily, but not, finally, disposed of — “Such exceptions occur only through one of the processes by which, from one session to another, a main motion can remain within the control of the assembly (that is, temporarily, but not finally, disposed of), so that the same motion can be considered at the later session.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 38:8 — “Such exceptions occur only through one of the processes by which, from one session to another, a main motion can remain within the control of the assembly (that is, temporarily, but not finally, disposed of), so that the same motion can be considered at the later session.”

**14.** `[C0066 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: Such exceptions occur only through one of the processes by which, from one session to another, a main motion can remain within the control of the assembly (that is, temporarily, but not _____), so that the same motion can be considered at the later session.

   B. primary
   C. finally, disposed of
   D. Limit or

   *Answer:* C) finally, disposed of. **15.** `[C0067 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): A _____ of an assembly, in the parliamentary sense, as mentioned above, is a person entitled to full participation in its proceedings, that is, as explained in 3 and 4, the right to attend meetings, to _____, to speak in debate, and to vote.

   *Answer:* make motions, member — “A member of an assembly, in the parliamentary sense, as mentioned above, is a person entitled to full participation in its proceedings, that is, as explained in 3 and 4, the right to attend meetings, to make motions, to speak in debate, and to vote.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 1:4 — “A member of an assembly, in the parliamentary sense, as mentioned above, is a person entitled to full participation in its proceedings, that is, as explained in 3 and 4, the right to attend meetings, to make motions, to speak in debate, and to vote.”

**16.** `[C0067 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: A member of an assembly, in the parliamentary sense, as mentioned above, is a person entitled to full participation in its proceedings, that is, as explained in 3 and 4, the right to attend meetings, to _____, to speak in debate, and to vote.

   B. make motions
   C. unanimous
   D. deliberative assembly

**17.** `[C0069 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): If two or more rise at about the same time, the general rule is that, all other things being equal, the member who rose and addressed the chair first _____ is entitled to be recognized.

   *Answer:* after the floor was yielded — “If two or more rise at about the same time, the general rule is that, all other things being equal, the member who rose and addressed the chair first after the floor was yielded is entitled to be recognized.”. **19.** `[C0086 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): In the ordinary case, especially under new business, there are six essential steps—three by which the motion is _____, and three in the _____ of the motion.

**21.** `[C0088 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): A deliberative assembly that has not adopted any rules is _____ly understood to hold itself bound by the rules and customs of the _____—or common parliamentary law (as discussed in the Introduction)—to the extent that there is agreement in the meeting body as to what these rules and practices are.

   *Answer:* general parliamentary law, common — “A deliberative assembly that has not adopted any rules is commonly understood to hold itself bound by the rules and customs of the general parliamentary law—or common parliamentary law (as discussed in the Introduction)—to the extent that there is agreement in the meeting body as to what these rules and practices are.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 1:5 — “A deliberative assembly that has not adopted any rules is commonly understood to hold itself bound by the rules and customs of the general parliamentary law—or common parliamentary law (as discussed in the Introduction)—to the extent that there is agreement in the meeting body as to what these rules and practices are.”

**22.** `[C0088 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: A deliberative assembly that has not adopted any rules is commonly understood to hold itself bound by the rules and customs of the _____—or common parliamentary law (as discussed in the Introduction)—to the extent that there is agreement in the meeting body as to what these rules and practices are.

   B. general parliamentary law
   C. program
   D. yeas and nays,

   *Answer:* B) general parliamentary law. **23.** `[C0118 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): When a _____ who has legitimately obtained the floor offers a motion which is not in order, the chair may be able, in certain instances, to suggest an alternative motion which _____ be in order and would carry out the desired intent to the satisfaction of the maker.

   *Answer:* member, would — “When a member who has legitimately obtained the floor offers a motion which is not in order, the chair may be able, in certain instances, to suggest an alternative motion which would be in order and would carry out the desired intent to the satisfaction of the maker.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 4:17 — “When a member who has legitimately obtained the floor offers a motion which is not in order, the chair may be able, in certain instances, to suggest an alternative motion which would be in order and would carry out the desired intent to the satisfaction of the maker.”

**27.** `[C0120 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): However, if a customary practice is or becomes in conflict with the parliamentary authority or any written rule, and a _____ (23) citing the conflict is raised at any time, the custom falls to the ground, and the conflicting provision in the parliamentary authority or written rule must thereafter be complied with.

   *Answer:* Point of Order — “However, if a customary practice is or becomes in conflict with the parliamentary authority or any written rule, and a Point of Order (23) citing the conflict is raised at any time, the custom falls to the ground, and the conflicting provision in the parliamentary authority or written rule must thereafter be complied with.”. **74.** `[C0438 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The minimum essential officers for the conduct of business in a deliberative assembly are a _____ officer, who conducts the meeting and sees that the rules are observed, and a _____, or clerk, who makes a written record of what is done—usually called “the minutes.” If the officers are members of the assembly—as they usually are in ordinary societies—they are counted in determining whether a quorum is present.

   *Answer:* presiding, secretary — “The minimum essential officers for the conduct of business in a deliberative assembly are a presiding officer, who conducts the meeting and sees that the rules are observed, and a secretary, or clerk, who makes a written record of what is done—usually called “the minutes.” If the officers are members of the assembly—as they usually are in ordinary societies—they are counted in determining whether a quorum is present.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 3:6 — “The minimum essential officers for the conduct of business in a deliberative assembly are a presiding officer, who conducts the meeting and sees that the rules are observed, and a secretary, or clerk, who makes a written record of what is done—usually called “the minutes.” If the officers are members of the assembly—as they usually are in ordinary societies—they are counted in determining whether a quorum is present.”

   C. Question
   D. Any Other Privilege

   *Answer:* B) deliberative. See RONR (12th ed.) 43:1 — “In a deliberative assembly, this term applies to discussion on the merits of a pending question—that is, whether the proposal under consideration should, or should not, be agreed to.”

See RONR (12th ed.) 4:28 — “A member who has spoken twice on a particular question on the same day has exhausted his right to debate that question for that day.”

   *Answer:* does — “It is common, especially in conventions, to hear the word recess also applied to a longer break that does terminate a meeting and that consequently should be understood as an adjournment, as in “to recess until tomorrow.” On the other hand, assemblies sometimes “adjourn” or provide in the program or agenda for an “adjournment” when only a short recess is intended.”.    *Answer:* session, meeting — “When common expressions such as “regular [or “stated”] meeting,” “special [or “called”] meeting,” and “annual meeting” (see below) are used in the bylaws, rules, or resolutions adopted by an organization, the word meeting is understood to mean session in the parliamentary sense, and therefore covers all adjourned meetings.”.    *Answer:* B) the chair. See RONR (12th ed.) 47:5 — “The presiding officer of an assembly ordinarily is called the chairman when no special title has been assigned, or in a body not permanently organized, such as a mass meeting (53).”

**199.** `[C1067 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The only way for business to be carried over directly from one session to some later regular session _____ the next regular business session is by being referred to a committee that will report at that later session.

   *Answer:* beyond — “The only way for business to be carried over directly from one session to some later regular session beyond the next regular business session is by being referred to a committee that will report at that later session.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 9:10 — “The only way for business to be carried over directly from one session to some later regular session beyond the next regular business session is by being referred to a committee that will report at that later session.”

**200.** `[C1067 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: The only way for business to be carried over directly from one session to some later regular session _____ the next regular business session is by being referred to a committee that will report at that later session.
   A. Roll-Call Vote
   B. beyond
   C. Reconsider
   D. Call for the Orders of

   *Answer:* B) beyond. See RONR (12th ed.) 9:10 — “The only way for business to be carried over directly from one session to some later regular session beyond the next regular business session is by being referred to a committee that will report at that later session.”

**201.** `[C1105 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The official record of the proceedings of a deliberative assembly is usually called the _____ or sometimes— particularly in legislative bodies—the _____.

   *Answer:* minutes,, journal — “The official record of the proceedings of a deliberative assembly is usually called the minutes, or sometimes— particularly in legislative bodies—the journal.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 48:1 — “The official record of the proceedings of a deliberative assembly is usually called the minutes, or sometimes— particularly in legislative bodies—the journal.”

**202.** `[C1105 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: The official record of the proceedings of a deliberative assembly is usually called the minutes, or sometimes— particularly in legislative bodies—the _____.

   *Answer:* B) journal. See RONR (12th ed.) 48:1 — “The official record of the proceedings of a deliberative assembly is usually called the minutes, or sometimes— particularly in legislative bodies—the journal.”

**203.** `[C1108 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The order of business of a convention is known as the _____, or the _____, depending on whether it is interwoven with, or separate from, the overall schedule of convention meetings, events, etc.

## Domain 5: Voting, Nominations, and Elections

**1.** `[C0002 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): Taking a vote by _____ (or by _____ as it is also called) has the effect of placing on the record how each member, or sometimes each delegation, votes;

   *Answer:* roll call, yeas and nays, — “Taking a vote by roll call (or by yeas and nays, as it is also called) has the effect of placing on the record how each member, or sometimes each delegation, votes;”. See RONR (12th ed.) 45:45 — “Taking a vote by roll call (or by yeas and nays, as it is also called) has the effect of placing on the record how each member, or sometimes each delegation, votes;”

   C. yeas and nays,
   D. precedence of motions
