## Domain 6: Being and Serving as a Professional Parliamentarian and Teaching Parliamentary Procedure

**1.** `[C0021 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): A specification states _____ _____ which, if true, constitutes an instance of the offense indicated in the charge.

   *Answer:* done, what the accused is alleged to have — “A specification states what the accused is alleged to have done which, if true, constitutes an instance of the offense indicated in the charge.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 63:24 — “A specification states what the accused is alleged to have done which, if true, constitutes an instance of the offense indicated in the charge.”

**2.** `[C0021 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: A specification states what the accused is alleged to have _____ which, if true, constitutes an instance of the offense indicated in the charge.
   A. done
   B. Subsidiary motions
   C. For Information
   D. on the Table

   *Answer:* A) done. See RONR (12th ed.) 63:24 — “A specification states what the accused is alleged to have done which, if true, constitutes an instance of the offense indicated in the charge.”

**3.** `[C0175 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): So, if the chair ignores a member seeking the floor while entitled to it, ignores a properly made nondilatory motion, “gavels through” a motion in an improper attempt to cut off debate, or violates any other rule, any member may immediately raise a _____.

   *Answer:* Point of Order — “So, if the chair ignores a member seeking the floor while entitled to it, ignores a properly made nondilatory motion, “gavels through” a motion in an improper attempt to cut off debate, or violates any other rule, any member may immediately raise a Point of Order.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 62:4 — “So, if the chair ignores a member seeking the floor while entitled to it, ignores a properly made nondilatory motion, “gavels through” a motion in an improper attempt to cut off debate, or violates any other rule, any member may immediately raise a Point of Order.”

**4.** `[C0175 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: So, if the chair ignores a member seeking the floor while entitled to it, ignores a properly made nondilatory motion, “gavels through” a motion in an improper attempt to cut off debate, or violates any other rule, any member may immediately raise a _____.
   A. general parliamentary law
   B. Point of Order
   C. Strike Out
   D. For Permission (or Leave) to

   *Answer:* B) Point of Order. See RONR (12th ed.) 62:4 — “So, if the chair ignores a member seeking the floor while entitled to it, ignores a properly made nondilatory motion, “gavels through” a motion in an improper attempt to cut off debate, or violates any other rule, any member may immediately raise a Point of Order.”

**5.** `[C0224 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): To raise a _____, a member rises and, without waiting to be recognized, immediately addresses the chair, saying, “I rise to a point of order,” or simply, “Point of order!” The chair must then ask the member to state the point;

   *Answer:* Point of Order — “To raise a Point of Order, a member rises and, without waiting to be recognized, immediately addresses the chair, saying, “I rise to a point of order,” or simply, “Point of order!” The chair must then ask the member to state the point;”. ## Domain 7: Boards and Committees, and Writing and Interpreting Bylaws

**1.** `[C0049 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The _____ and its two alternate forms, the _____ (or consideration as if in committee of the whole) and informal consideration, are devices that enable the full assembly to give detailed consideration to a matter under conditions of freedom somewhat like those of a committee.

   *Answer:* quasi committee of the whole, committee of the whole — “The committee of the whole and its two alternate forms, the quasi committee of the whole (or consideration as if in committee of the whole) and informal consideration, are devices that enable the full assembly to give detailed consideration to a matter under conditions of freedom somewhat like those of a committee.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 52:1 — “The committee of the whole and its two alternate forms, the quasi committee of the whole (or consideration as if in committee of the whole) and informal consideration, are devices that enable the full assembly to give detailed consideration to a matter under conditions of freedom somewhat like those of a committee.”

**2.** `[C0049 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: The committee of the whole and its two alternate forms, the _____ (or consideration as if in committee of the whole) and informal consideration, are devices that enable the full assembly to give detailed consideration to a matter under conditions of freedom somewhat like those of a committee.
   A. originating in the committee
   B. opinion
   C. Articles of Association
   D. quasi committee of the whole

   *Answer:* D) quasi committee of the whole. See RONR (12th ed.) 52:1 — “The committee of the whole and its two alternate forms, the quasi committee of the whole (or consideration as if in committee of the whole) and informal consideration, are devices that enable the full assembly to give detailed consideration to a matter under conditions of freedom somewhat like those of a committee.”

**3.** `[C0058 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): In the case of an unincorporated society, a resolution should be prepared, such as: “_____ That the X Society be dissolved as of March 31, 20.” This resolution may be preceded by a preamble setting forth the reasons for the dissolution.

   *Answer:* Resolved, — “In the case of an unincorporated society, a resolution should be prepared, such as: “Resolved, That the X Society be dissolved as of March 31, 20.” This resolution may be preceded by a preamble setting forth the reasons for the dissolution.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 55:6 — “In the case of an unincorporated society, a resolution should be prepared, such as: “Resolved, That the X Society be dissolved as of March 31, 20.” This resolution may be preceded by a preamble setting forth the reasons for the dissolution.”

**4.** `[C0058 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: In the case of an unincorporated society, a resolution should be prepared, such as: “_____ That the X Society be dissolved as of March 31, 20.” This resolution may be preceded by a preamble setting forth the reasons for the dissolution.
   A. Adjourned Meeting
   B. after the floor
   C. Resolved,
   D. except

   *Answer:* C) Resolved,. See RONR (12th ed.) 55:6 — “In the case of an unincorporated society, a resolution should be prepared, such as: “Resolved, That the X Society be dissolved as of March 31, 20.” This resolution may be preceded by a preamble setting forth the reasons for the dissolution.”

**5.** `[C0070 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The more traditional aids to the crystallization of opinion in societies have been, simply, to take a _____ or to refer the matter to a committee—often a large committee composed of members representing differing views in the society, such as a committee of the whole or one of its alternate forms.

   *Answer:* Recess — “The more traditional aids to the crystallization of opinion in societies have been, simply, to take a Recess or to refer the matter to a committee—often a large committee composed of members representing differing views in the society, such as a committee of the whole or one of its alternate forms.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 52:28 — “The more traditional aids to the crystallization of opinion in societies have been, simply, to take a Recess or to refer the matter to a committee—often a large committee composed of members representing differing views in the society, such as a committee of the whole or one of its alternate forms.”

**6.** `[C0070 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: The more traditional aids to the crystallization of opinion in societies have been, simply, to take a _____ or to refer the matter to a committee—often a large committee composed of members representing differing views in the society, such as a committee of the whole or one of its alternate forms.
   A. dispense with
   B. adopt, accept,
   C. debate
   D. Recess

   *Answer:* D) Recess. See RONR (12th ed.) 52:28 — “The more traditional aids to the crystallization of opinion in societies have been, simply, to take a Recess or to refer the matter to a committee—often a large committee composed of members representing differing views in the society, such as a committee of the whole or one of its alternate forms.”

   *Answer:* amend — “The wording of this article should avoid redundant phraseology such as “amend, alter, add to, or repeal,” or “alter or amend,” or “amend or in any way change.” The word amend covers any change, whether a word or a paragraph is to be added, struck out, or replaced, or whether a new set of articles is to be substituted for the old one.”. **57.** `[C0908 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The term _____ or house of _____, is often applied particularly in the case of learned or professional associations, to distinguish the voting body of delegates from large numbers of other members of the constituent units, who come to the convention to attend seminars, workshops, educational or social activities, or the like.

   *Answer:* representatives, house of delegates, — “The term house of delegates, or house of representatives, is often applied particularly in the case of learned or professional associations, to distinguish the voting body of delegates from large numbers of other members of the constituent units, who come to the convention to attend seminars, workshops, educational or social activities, or the like.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 58:2 — “The term house of delegates, or house of representatives, is often applied particularly in the case of learned or professional associations, to distinguish the voting body of delegates from large numbers of other members of the constituent units, who come to the convention to attend seminars, workshops, educational or social activities, or the like.”

**58.** `[C0908 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: The term _____ or house of representatives, is often applied particularly in the case of learned or professional associations, to distinguish the voting body of delegates from large numbers of other members of the constituent units, who come to the convention to attend seminars, workshops, educational or social activities, or the like.
   A. standing rule of
   B. Division of the
   C. after
   D. house of delegates,

   *Answer:* D) house of delegates,. See RONR (12th ed.) 58:2 — “The term house of delegates, or house of representatives, is often applied particularly in the case of learned or professional associations, to distinguish the voting body of delegates from large numbers of other members of the constituent units, who come to the convention to attend seminars, workshops, educational or social activities, or the like.”

**59.** `[C0980 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The Resolutions Committee—also sometimes called the _____ or, in certain cases described below, the _____—has as its basic purpose the screening of all original main motions (10) that have not been screened by another committee and that come—or are to come—before the convention.

   *Answer:* Platform Committee, Reference Committee — “The Resolutions Committee—also sometimes called the Reference Committee or, in certain cases described below, the Platform Committee—has as its basic purpose the screening of all original main motions (10) that have not been screened by another committee and that come—or are to come—before the convention.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 59:67 — “The Resolutions Committee—also sometimes called the Reference Committee or, in certain cases described below, the Platform Committee—has as its basic purpose the screening of all original main motions (10) that have not been screened by another committee and that come—or are to come—before the convention.”

**60.** `[C0980 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: The Resolutions Committee—also sometimes called the _____ or, in certain cases described below, the Platform Committee—has as its basic purpose the screening of all original main motions (10) that have not been screened by another committee and that come—or are to come—before the convention.
   A. advance
   B. Reference Committee
   C. standard descriptive characteristics
   D. Rules

   *Answer:* B) Reference Committee. See RONR (12th ed.) 59:67 — “The Resolutions Committee—also sometimes called the Reference Committee or, in certain cases described below, the Platform Committee—has as its basic purpose the screening of all original main motions (10) that have not been screened by another committee and that come—or are to come—before the convention.”

**61.** `[C1044 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): A special (_____ or _____) committee is a committee appointed, as the need arises, to carry out a specified task, at the completion of which—that is, on presentation of its final report to the assembly—it automatically ceases to exist.

   *Answer:* ad hoc, select, — “A special (select, or ad hoc) committee is a committee appointed, as the need arises, to carry out a specified task, at the completion of which—that is, on presentation of its final report to the assembly—it automatically ceases to exist.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 50:10 — “A special (select, or ad hoc) committee is a committee appointed, as the need arises, to carry out a specified task, at the completion of which—that is, on presentation of its final report to the assembly—it automatically ceases to exist.”

**62.** `[C1044 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: A special (_____ or ad hoc) committee is a committee appointed, as the need arises, to carry out a specified task, at the completion of which—that is, on presentation of its final report to the assembly—it automatically ceases to exist.
   A. Call
   B. select,
   C. functioning of a society or assembly
   D. The motion to amend by striking

   *Answer:* B) select,. See RONR (12th ed.) 50:10 — “A special (select, or ad hoc) committee is a committee appointed, as the need arises, to carry out a specified task, at the completion of which—that is, on presentation of its final report to the assembly—it automatically ceases to exist.”

**63.** `[C1062 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): As applied to an assembly’s action with respect to board or committee reports or any of their contents, the expressions _____ accept, and _____ are all equivalent—that is, the text adopted becomes in effect the act or statement of the assembly.

   *Answer:* adopt,, agree to — “As applied to an assembly’s action with respect to board or committee reports or any of their contents, the expressions adopt, accept, and agree to are all equivalent—that is, the text adopted becomes in effect the act or statement of the assembly.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 51:14 — “As applied to an assembly’s action with respect to board or committee reports or any of their contents, the expressions adopt, accept, and agree to are all equivalent—that is, the text adopted becomes in effect the act or statement of the assembly.”

**64.** `[C1062 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: As applied to an assembly’s action with respect to board or committee reports or any of their contents, the expressions _____ and agree to are all equivalent—that is, the text adopted becomes in effect the act or statement of the assembly.
   A. program
   B. of Order
   C. incidental
   D. adopt, accept,

   *Answer:* D) adopt, accept,. See RONR (12th ed.) 51:14 — “As applied to an assembly’s action with respect to board or committee reports or any of their contents, the expressions adopt, accept, and agree to are all equivalent—that is, the text adopted becomes in effect the act or statement of the assembly.”

**65.** `[C1076 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): The rules contained in the current edition of _____ _____ shall govern the convention in all cases to which they are applicable and in which they are not inconsistent with the bylaws of the Society [or “Federation,” “Association,” etc.] and these standing rules.

   *Answer:* Robert’s Rules of, Order Newly Revised — “The rules contained in the current edition of Robert’s Rules of Order Newly Revised shall govern the convention in all cases to which they are applicable and in which they are not inconsistent with the bylaws of the Society [or “Federation,” “Association,” etc.] and these standing rules.”. See RONR (12th ed.) 59:47 — “The rules contained in the current edition of Robert’s Rules of Order Newly Revised shall govern the convention in all cases to which they are applicable and in which they are not inconsistent with the bylaws of the Society [or “Federation,” “Association,” etc.] and these standing rules.”

**66.** `[C1076 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: The rules contained in the current edition of _____ Order Newly Revised shall govern the convention in all cases to which they are applicable and in which they are not inconsistent with the bylaws of the Society [or “Federation,” “Association,” etc.] and these standing rules.
   A. Parliamentary Inquiry
   B. Robert’s Rules of
   C. Raise a Question of Privilege
   D. Raise a Question

   *Answer:* B) Robert’s Rules of. See RONR (12th ed.) 59:47 — “The rules contained in the current edition of Robert’s Rules of Order Newly Revised shall govern the convention in all cases to which they are applicable and in which they are not inconsistent with the bylaws of the Society [or “Federation,” “Association,” etc.] and these standing rules.”

**67.** `[C1096 · Cloze recall]` Fill the blank(s): A reporting member _____ or _____ a report on behalf of a board or a committee when, having been assigned the floor for such a purpose in a meeting, he does one of the following things (depending on the nature of the report and other conditions): (a) renders the report orally, if it is not in writing;

   *Answer:* makes, presents — “A reporting member makes or presents a report on behalf of a board or a committee when, having been assigned the floor for such a purpose in a meeting, he does one of the following things (depending on the nature of the report and other conditions): (a) renders the report orally, if it is not in writing;”. See RONR (12th ed.) 51:9 — “A reporting member makes or presents a report on behalf of a board or a committee when, having been assigned the floor for such a purpose in a meeting, he does one of the following things (depending on the nature of the report and other conditions): (a) renders the report orally, if it is not in writing;”

**68.** `[C1096 · Applied multiple-choice]` Fill in the blank: When the assembly hears the report thus read or orally rendered, it _____ the report.
   A. division
   B. meeting
   C. precedence of motions
   D. receives

   *Answer:* D) receives. See RONR (12th ed.) 51:9 — “When the assembly hears the report thus read or orally rendered, it receives the report.”
